72pt}.c61{padding:0;margin:0}.c157{text-decoration:none;vertical-align:baseline}.c120{height:37.5pt}.c27{height:11pt}.c70{color:#0000ff}.c72{height:27.8pt}.c98{height:28.7pt}.c77{font-size:9pt}.c40{background-color:#ffffff}.c168{color:#1155cc}.c104{height:26.2pt}.c59{color:#24292e}.c185{height:15.7pt}.c64{margin-left:72pt}.c100{background-color:#fff2cc}.c67{font-family:"Arial"}.c117{color:#ff0000}.c151{background-color:#c9d1d9}.c76{height:17.2pt}.c133{margin-left:108pt}.c155{background-color:#cccccc}.c58{font-style:italic}.c45{color:#0d1117}.c32{font-weight:700}.c69{height:0pt}.c20{font-size:8pt}.c138{color:#a31515}.c41{height:15.8pt}.title{padding-top:0pt;color:#000000;font-size:26pt;padding-bottom:3pt;font-family:"Arial";line-height:1.15;page-break-after:avoid;orphans:2;widows:2;text-align:left}.subtitle{padding-top:0pt;color:#666666;font-size:15pt;padding-bottom:16pt;font-family:"Arial";line-height:1.15;page-break-after:avoid;orphans:2;widows:2;text-align:left}li{color:#000000;font-size:11pt;font-family:"Arial"}p{margin:0;color:#000000;font-size:11pt;font-family:"Arial"}h1{padding-top:20pt;color:#000000;font-size:20pt;padding-bottom:6pt;font-family:"Arial";line-height:1.15;page-break-after:avoid;orphans:2;widows:2;text-align:left}h2{padding-top:18pt;color:#000000;font-size:16pt;padding-bottom:6pt;font-family:"Arial";line-height:1.15;page-break-after:avoid;orphans:2;widows:2;text-align:left}h3{padding-top:16pt;color:#434343;font-size:14pt;padding-bottom:4pt;font-family:"Arial";line-height:1.15;page-break-after:avoid;orphans:2;widows:2;text-align:left}h4{padding-top:14pt;color:#666666;font-size:12pt;padding-bottom:4pt;font-family:"Arial";line-height:1.15;page-break-after:avoid;orphans:2;widows:2;text-align:left}h5{padding-top:12pt;color:#666666;font-size:11pt;padding-bottom:4pt;font-family:"Arial";line-height:1.15;page-break-after:avoid;orphans:2;widows:2;text-align:left}h6{padding-top:12pt;color:#666666;font-size:11pt;padding-bottom:4pt;font-family:"Arial";line-height:1.15;page-break-after:avoid;font-style:italic;orphans:2;widows:2;text-align:left}
</style>
</head>
<body class="c40 c167 doc-content">
<p class="c8">
<span class="c36 c42 c32">
Our Progress: A Chronology
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420211908&amp;usg=AOvVaw0WFmnGCYiZrBh-01Mhuu3_">MacroPlacement</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;is an open, transparent effort to provide a public, baseline implementation of </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420212483&amp;usg=AOvVaw2qKY-q2BtXsZPZZMtHgNJY">Google Brain&rsquo;s Circuit Training</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;(Morpheus) deep RL-based placement method. &nbsp;In this repo, &nbsp;we aim to achieve the following.</span>
</p>
<ul class="c61 lst-kix_6pqawvsimeex-0 start">
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c36 c34">We want to enable anyone to perform RL-based macro placement on their own design, starting from design RTL files.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c36 c34">We want to enable anyone to train their own RL models based on their own designs in any design enablements, starting from design RTL files.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34">We want to demystify important aspects of the </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-021-03544-w&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420213421&amp;usg=AOvVaw1RIrJr1oYSSaz5noZGCdzh">Google Nature paper</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">, including aspects unavailable in </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420213818&amp;usg=AOvVaw0JXcLA2xzs8vKTyfbOBRv8">Circuit Training</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;and aspects where the Nature paper and Circuit Training clearly diverge, in order to help researchers and users better understand the methodology.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34">We want to apply learnings from the community&rsquo;s collective experiences with the Google Brain team&rsquo;s arXiv result, Nature paper and Circuit Training repo &ndash; and demonstrate how communication of research results might be improved in our community going forward. &nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34 c70 c58 c157">A clear theme from the past months&rsquo; experience: &nbsp;&ldquo;There is no substitute for source code.&rdquo;</span>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c36 c34">In order to achieve the above goals, &nbsp;our initial focus has been on the following efforts.</span>
</p>
<ul class="c61 lst-kix_r9phsp2ympsl-0 start">
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c42 c32">Generating correct inputs and setup for Circuit Training.</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;Since Circuit Training uses protocol buffer format to represent designs, we must translate standard LEF/DEF representation to the protocol buffer format. We must also determine how to correctly feed all necessary design information into the </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420215137&amp;usg=AOvVaw3-paH9pCh6GMLmKC3LMZGo">Google Brain&rsquo;s Circuit Training</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp; flow, e.g., halo width, canvas size, and constraints. &nbsp;If we accomplish this, then we can run </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420215631&amp;usg=AOvVaw1K3hS6VXRMdgF41sB6TQWR">Google Brain&rsquo;s Circuit Training</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;to train our own RL models or perform RL-based macro placement for our own designs.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c42 c32">Replicating important but missing parts of the </span>
<span class="c85 c42 c40 c32">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-021-03544-w&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420216285&amp;usg=AOvVaw3PR4Y7vgqmqdiivk9UmhnP">Google Nature paper</a>
</span>
<span class="c42 c32">.</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;Several aspects of Circuit Training are not clearly documented in the Nature paper, nor in the code and scripts that are visible in Circuit Training. Over time, these have included hypergraph-to-graph conversion; gridding, grouping and clustering; force-directed placement; various hyperparameter settings; and more. As we keep moving forward, based on our experiments and continued Q&amp;A and feedback from Google, we will summarize the miscorrelations between the </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-021-03544-w&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420216801&amp;usg=AOvVaw1C5KK90LyQNUTIjauhVZSg">Google Nature paper</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;and </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420217199&amp;usg=AOvVaw3gBomGIGIVkdOnV5tG0xcE">Google Brain&rsquo;s Circuit Training</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">, as well as corrective steps. In this way, the Circuit Training methodology and the results published in the Nature paper can be better understood by all.</span>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c42 c32">June 6 - Aug 5: </span>
<span class="c34 c40">We have developed and made publicly available the SP&amp;R </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Flows&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420218089&amp;usg=AOvVaw1QZ43KZjCvha3cU8sE1yW0">flow</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;using commercial tools Cadence Genus and Innovus, and open-source tools Yosys and OpenROAD, for </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Testcases/ariane136&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420218567&amp;usg=AOvVaw0vzpiafAub6UXVOh-rme_I">Ariane</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;(two variants &ndash; one with </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Testcases/ariane136&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420219008&amp;usg=AOvVaw3QHrLwawxY6coVuMeh5gH8">136 SRAMs</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;and another with </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Testcases/ariane133&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420219478&amp;usg=AOvVaw1bA7hrVhal8y1ahcImgvmI">133 SRAMs</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">), </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Testcases/mempool&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420219913&amp;usg=AOvVaw2TNIvOxNu5QWMRkbyfGRTM">MemPool tile</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;and </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Testcases/nvdla&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420220329&amp;usg=AOvVaw2JI_5iL855DK6K0cCOVkQV">NVDLA</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;designs on </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Enablements/NanGate45&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420220799&amp;usg=AOvVaw3bPDK3nryHVE3NZ8e6dsIA">NanGate45</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">, </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Enablements/ASAP7&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420221269&amp;usg=AOvVaw2do6U9q62qEqDcJRUcCj2N">ASAP7</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;and </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Enablements/SKY130HD&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420221737&amp;usg=AOvVaw3NZy5g7ToSZKAeEJTYpM2Y">SKY130HD</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;open enablement. </span>
<span class="c34 c40 c117">We applaud and thank Cadence Design Systems for allowing their tool runscripts to be shared openly by researchers, enabling reproducibility of results obtained via use of Cadence tools</span>
<span class="c34 c40 c59">. This was an important milestone for the EDA research community. </span>
<span class="c34 c40">Please see Dr. David Junkin&rsquo;s </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://open-source-eda-birds-of-a-feather.github.io/doc/slides/BOAF-Junkin-DAC-Presentation.pdf&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420222481&amp;usg=AOvVaw3ICbnPtyv9_xubVB7Njg3Y">presentation</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;at the recent DAC-2022 &ldquo;Open-Source EDA and Benchmarking Summit&rdquo; birds-of-a-feather </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://open-source-eda-birds-of-a-feather.github.io/&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420222995&amp;usg=AOvVaw0opDb9CdBxmiy6e6aV2hTd">meeting</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">. </span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c35 c34">The following describes our learning related to testcase generation and its implementation using different tools on different platforms.</span>
</p>
<ol class="c61 lst-kix_z5d93gwj9bm3-0 start" start="1">
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c40">The </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-021-03544-w&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420223942&amp;usg=AOvVaw1SKVFqnZipMR6Fr3dXH1tt">Google Nature paper</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;uses the Ariane testcase (contains 133 256x16-bit SRAMs) for their experiment. </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/Testcases/ariane136%23netlist-preparation-of-ariane-136-macro-version&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420224478&amp;usg=AOvVaw2oftR27AE9l-jIsg0MjJTC">Here</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;we show that just instantiating 256x16 bit SRAMs results in 136 SRAMs in the synthesized netlist. Based on our investigations, we have provided the </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/Testcases/ariane133%23netlist-preparation-of-ariane-133-macro-version&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420225053&amp;usg=AOvVaw3am0An6GlENuwxGPHkERhy">detailed steps</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;to convert the Ariane design with 136 SRAMs to a Ariane design with 133 SRAMs.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c40">We provide the required SRAM lef, lib along with the description to reproduce the provided SRAMs or generate a new SRAM for each </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Enablements/&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420225784&amp;usg=AOvVaw2E7MTobjZcc47gL_xzepDd">enablement</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c40">The SKY130HD enablement has only five metal layers, while SRAMs have routing up through the M4 layer. This causes P&amp;R failure due to very high routing congestion. We therefore developed FakeStack-extended P&amp;R enablement, where we replicate the first four metal layers to generate a nine metal layer enablement. We call this </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Enablements/SKY130HD%23sky130hd-fakestack-sky130hd-library-bsg_fakeram-memory-generation-9m-fakestack&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420226636&amp;usg=AOvVaw1-DxAjaaOjgQUVsmdf5oMk">SKY130HD-FakeStack</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;and have used it to implement our testcases. We also provide a </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/blob/flow_scripts/Enablements/SKY130HD/lef/genTechLef.tcl&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420227159&amp;usg=AOvVaw1qMiOWz9Wc2t_6eNCHf9ln">script</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;for researchers to generate FakeStack enablements with different configurations.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c40">We provide power grid generation </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/blob/flow_scripts/Flows/util/pdn_flow.tcl&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420227781&amp;usg=AOvVaw39UvZS5PxBK8h9-NbLpjA5">scripts</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;for Cadence Innovus. During the power grid (PG) generation process we made sure the routing resource used by the PG is in the range of ~20%, matching the guidance given in Circuit Training.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c40">Also we provide an Innovus Tcl </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/blob/flow_scripts/Flows/util/extract_report.tcl&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420228396&amp;usg=AOvVaw0ccfFDrauLf0_KiQFUi4Ey">script</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;to extract the metrics reported in Table 1 of &ldquo;</span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://www.nature.com/articles/s41586-021-03544-w&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420228797&amp;usg=AOvVaw33PZzptN_83EoONHHIQwei">A graph placement methodology for fast chip design</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&rdquo;, </span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">at three stages of the post-floorplanning P&amp;R flow, i.e., pre-CTS, post-CTSOpt, and post-RouteOpt (final).</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;This </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/blob/flow_scripts/Flows/util/extract_report.tcl&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420229314&amp;usg=AOvVaw3QFf0enPEuURYM-po-QrVI">script</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;is included in the P&amp;R flow. The extracted metrics for all of our designs, on different enablements, are available </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/ExperimentalData&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420229787&amp;usg=AOvVaw0381VBRUVKCP1D6VcT6QZB">here</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">.</span>
</li>
</ol>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c163">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.7ozu5wy34cbb">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c32">June 10: </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/main/circuit_training/grouping/grouper.py&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420230755&amp;usg=AOvVaw3wHgf4wWuB-H0CPQIfz402">grouper.py</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;was released in CircuitTraining. </span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">This revealed that protobuf input to the hypergraph clustering into soft macros included the (x,y) locations of the nodes.</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;(A </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/main/circuit_training/grouping/grouper.py&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420231415&amp;usg=AOvVaw38j_3jxEnmAOIyVdf3BWIL">grouper.py</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;script had been shown to Prof. Kahng during a meeting at Google on May 19.) The use of (x,y) locations from a physical synthesis tool was very unexpected, since it is not mentioned in &ldquo;Methods&rdquo; or other descriptions given in the Nature paper. We raised </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/issues/25%23issue-1268683034&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420231776&amp;usg=AOvVaw3qXvwfT_i3ycjU5vPa4PUu">issue #25</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;to get clarification about this. [</span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">July 10: </span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;The </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/main/circuit_training/grouping/README.md%23faq&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420232200&amp;usg=AOvVaw3rxMFXsjR11FOrSXEcTfIU">README</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;added to </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/tree/main/circuit_training/grouping&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420232496&amp;usg=AOvVaw3sG_kVoOYxpQ82a4c2Gff8">the grouping area</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;of CircuitTraining confirmed that the input netlist has all of its nodes </span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">already placed</span>
<span class="c35 c34">.]</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c34 c40">We currently use the physical synthesis tool </span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">Cadence Genus iSpatial</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;to obtain (x,y) placed locations per instance as part of the input to Grouping. The Genus iSpatial post-physical-synthesis netlist is the starting point for how we produce the clustered netlist and the *.plc file which we provide as open inputs to CircuitTraining. From post-physical-synthesis netlist to clustered netlist generation can be divided into the following steps, which we have implemented as open-source in our CodeElements area:</span>
</p>
<ol class="c61 lst-kix_63lqho3p6504-0 start" start="1">
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">June 6</span>
<span class="c34 c40">: </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/CodeElements/Gridding&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420233663&amp;usg=AOvVaw01TJvVVzHj00oiCVtLV7w-">Gridding</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;determines a dissection of the layout canvas into some number of rows and some number of columns of gridcells.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">June 10</span>
<span class="c34 c40">: </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/CodeElements/Grouping&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420234401&amp;usg=AOvVaw2TA-o3nlf0AeYED5DHe5bS">Grouping</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;groups closely-related logic with the corresponding hard macros and clumps of IOs.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">June 12:</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/CodeElements/Clustering&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420235116&amp;usg=AOvVaw3N1UvubpZwm_kj0-D8fspm">Clustering</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;clusters of millions of standard cells into a few thousand clusters (soft macros).</span>
</li>
</ol>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">June 22:</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;We added our </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/CodeElements/CodeFlowIntegration&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420235764&amp;usg=AOvVaw0t0cypbmcF4cdotKCTn-u5">flow-scripts</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;that run our gridding, grouping and clustering implementations to generate a final clustered netlist </span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">in protocol buffer format</span>
<span class="c34 c40">. Google&rsquo;s </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/main/docs/NETLIST_FORMAT.md&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420236287&amp;usg=AOvVaw1ZyF2SODshlUe99wYmBP-b">netlist protocol buffer format</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;documentation available in the </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420236548&amp;usg=AOvVaw2rfw_JBkw2efrH539e4fzG">CircuitTraining repo</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;was very helpful to our understanding of how to convert a placed netlist to protobuf format. Our </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/CodeElements/FormatTranslators&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420236804&amp;usg=AOvVaw0g-5YLoAPKUqI4xzq5xoe9">scripts</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;enable clustered netlists in protobuf format to be produced from placed netlists in either LEF/DEF or Bookshelf format.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">July 12: &nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34 c40">As stated in the &ldquo;What is your timeline?&rdquo; FAQ response [see also note [5] </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1vkPRgJEiLIyT22AkQNAxO8JtIKiL95diVdJ_O4AFtJ8/edit?usp%3Dsharing&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420237460&amp;usg=AOvVaw1JqZhqUyzByeZU_bU1I9tU">here</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">], we presented progress to date in this</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://open-source-eda-birds-of-a-feather.github.io/doc/slides/MacroPlacement-SpecPart-DAC-BOF-v5.pdf&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420238086&amp;usg=AOvVaw398MoEPu9qX43zdqtZYcVc">MacroPlacement talk</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;at the DAC-2022 &ldquo;Open-Source EDA and Benchmarking Summit&rdquo; birds-of-a-feather </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://open-source-eda-birds-of-a-feather.github.io/&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420238524&amp;usg=AOvVaw07_Ly8dwHauIOrGDPRBr6D">meeting</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">. </span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c34 c97 c117">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">July 26: &nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34 c70 c40">Replication of the wirelength component of proxy cost.</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34">The wirelength is similar to HPWL where given a netlist, we take the width and height and sum them up for each net. One caveat is that for soft macro pins, there could be a weight factor which implies the total connections between the source and sink pins. If not defined, the default value is 1. This weight factor needs to be multiplied with the sum of width and height to replicate Google&rsquo;s API. We provide the following table as a comparison between </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/CodeElements/Plc_client&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420239701&amp;usg=AOvVaw1WFyM8aim8AU0aeWUROlsk">our implementations</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;and Google&rsquo;s API.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<a id="t.037579025385bfe1fc4e411b9dbd339359881efd">

<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">July 31:</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;The </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/main/docs/NETLIST_FORMAT.md&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420246916&amp;usg=AOvVaw3qQW0m0pFH202_5EWTb6Bg">netlist protocol buffer format</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;documentation also helped us to write this Innovus-based &nbsp;</span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/blob/flow_scripts/Flows/util/gen_pb.tcl&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420247400&amp;usg=AOvVaw1bugIDlv7V9drGb_deKL2N">tcl script</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;which converts physical synthesized netlist to protobuf format in Innovus. &nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34 c40 c117">[This script was written and developed by ABKGroup students at UCSD. However, the underlying commands and reports are copyrighted by Cadence. We thank Cadence for granting permission to share our research to help promote and foster the next generation of innovators.]</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;We use this post-physical-synthesis protobuf netlist as input to the grouping code to generate the clustered netlist. Fixes that we made while running Google&rsquo;s grouping code resulted in </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/pull/33&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420248018&amp;usg=AOvVaw1oKV0Muo-ke0mUE73UREyq">this [08/01/2022] pull request</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">. [08/05/2022: Google&rsquo;s grouping code has been updated based on this </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/pull/33&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420248493&amp;usg=AOvVaw3ToavXrY1WrQtotmfjF9E1">PR</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">.]</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">July 22-August 4:</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;We shared with Google engineers our (flat) </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://drive.google.com/file/d/1dVltyKwjWcCAPRRKlcN2CRSeaxuaScPI/view?usp%3Dsharing&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420249285&amp;usg=AOvVaw0x2WAAjoAyjQA5RLm3JG-N">post-physical-synthesis-protobuf netlist (ariane.pb.txt)</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;of </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://drive.google.com/file/d/1BvqqSngFiWXk5WNAFDO8KMPq3eqI5THf/view?usp%3Dsharing&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420249702&amp;usg=AOvVaw0OMZ06xl1TlbGe9qerc2Ju">our Ariane design with 133 SRAMs on the NanGate45 platform</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">, along with the corresponding </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://drive.google.com/file/d/1dVltyKwjWcCAPRRKlcN2CRSeaxuaScPI/view?usp%3Dsharing&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420250100&amp;usg=AOvVaw15tam_KKrcW-IA-CllkVmz">clustered netlist and the legalized.plc file (clustered netlist: netlist.pb.txt)</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp; generated using the </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420250450&amp;usg=AOvVaw2zE8U4M86L2OV4bUJCYxxf">CircuitTraining grouping code</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">. The goal here was to verify our steps and setup up to this point. Also, we provide </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Flows/util&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420250827&amp;usg=AOvVaw3vyjfYNuwBJhX9NUjzsfJb">scripts</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;(using both our </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/CodeElements&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420251194&amp;usg=AOvVaw1fImz3ZU-8gUWNhKSgQcIt">CodeElements</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;and </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/tree/main/circuit_training/grouping&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420251594&amp;usg=AOvVaw26AI6xeA4BvsXQ8KMUwY0p">CT-grouping</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">) to integrate the clustered netlist generation with the SP&amp;R flow. </span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">August 5: </span>
<span class="c34 c40">The following table compares the clustering results for </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/Flows/NanGate45/ariane133&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420252406&amp;usg=AOvVaw1JjZtlz0VaWiC69yJNFFWE">Ariane133-NG45</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;design generated by the Google engineer (internally to Google) and the clustering results generated by us using </span>
<span class="c12 c40">

</span>
<span class="c35 c34">.</span>

<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">August 11: </span>
<span class="c34 c40">We received information from Google that when a standard cell has multiple outputs, it merges all of them in the protobuf netlist (example: a full adder cell would have its outputs merged). The possible vertices of a hyperedge are macro pins, ports, and standard cells. Our Innovus-based protobuf netlist generation </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/blob/flow_scripts/Flows/util/gen_pb.tcl&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420259509&amp;usg=AOvVaw2E3Zw1t9dQ8qhp1iH_f-_P">tcl script</a>
</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;takes care of this.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">August 15: </span>
<span class="c35 c34">We received information from Google engineers that in the proxy cost function, the density weight is set to 0.5 for their internal runs.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">August 17: </span>
<span class="c34 c40">The </span>
<span class="c36 c34">proxy wirelength cost which is usually a value between 0 and 1, is related to the HPWL we computed earlier. We deduce the formulation as the following:</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c64">
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 334.67px; height: 59.18px;">
<img alt="" src="images/image11.png" style="width: 334.67px; height: 59.18px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);" title="">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47">
<span class="c34 c58">|netlist|</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;is the total number of nets and it takes into account the weight factor defined on soft macro pins. Here is </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/CodeElements/Plc_client&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420260527&amp;usg=AOvVaw2KqaGaDfQYYXK0MzYjCzHs">our proxy wirelength</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;compared with Google&rsquo;s API:</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<a id="t.0dc37a5ea515107471f578205bf7129ce220720b">
</a>
<a id="t.2">

</p>

<p class="c52 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47">
<span class="c34 c70 c40">Replication of the density component of proxy cost.</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34">We now have a verified density cost computation. Density cost computation depends on gridcell density. Gridcell density is the ratio of the total area occupied by standard cells, soft macros and hard macros to the total area of the grid. If there are cell overlaps then it may result in grid density greater than one. To get the density cost, we take the average of the top 10% of the densest gridcells. Before outputting it, we multiply it by 0.5. Notice that this </span>
<span class="c42 c32">0.5 is not the &ldquo;weight&rdquo; of this cost function</span>
<span class="c36 c34">, but simply another factor applied besides the weight factor from the cost function.</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47 c133">
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 297.33px; height: 71.65px;">
<img alt="" src="images/image29.png" style="width: 297.33px; height: 71.65px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);" title="">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>

<p class="c52 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.gil8up925m8u">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">August 18:</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;The flat post-physical-synthesis protobuf netlist of </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/flow_scripts/Flows/NanGate45/ariane133/netlist/output_CT_Grouping&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420301254&amp;usg=AOvVaw3ehAyCDQbmMLgJT585fIMM">Ariane133-NanGate45</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;design is used as input to </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/tree/main/circuit_training/grouping&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420301625&amp;usg=AOvVaw22y8WbgBrMSh2m3CZI3RSJ">CT grouping</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;code to generate the clustered netlist. We then use this clustered netlist in Circuit Training. </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/main/circuit_training/environment/coordinate_descent_placer.py&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420301901&amp;usg=AOvVaw07Hx4F3RsOZWPNKkgVhjXr">Coordinate Descent</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;is (by </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/9e7097fa0c2a82030f43b298259941fc8ca6b7ae/circuit_training/learning/eval.py%23L50-L52&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420302371&amp;usg=AOvVaw0or7H7sdhSA2iISQ4TIXnC">default</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">) not applied to any macro placement solution. Here is the </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://tensorboard.dev/experiment/eCRHe29LQvi1sdAPD61Q6A/%23scalars&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420302663&amp;usg=AOvVaw3TY4xgMkayeI6jooaRIk0H">link</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;to our tensorboard. We ran Innovus P&amp;R starting from the macro placement generated using CT, through the end of detailed routing (RouteOpt) and collection of final PPA / &ldquo;Table 1&rdquo; metrics. Following are the metrics and screen shots of the P&amp;R </span>
<span class="c34 c40">database</span>
<span class="c34 c40">. </span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">Throughout the SP&amp;R flow, the target clock period is 4ns. </span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;The power grid overhead is 18.46% in the actual P&amp;R setup, matching the </span>
<span class="c34">18% </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/9e7097fa0c2a82030f43b298259941fc8ca6b7ae/circuit_training/environment/placement_util.py%23L183-L186&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420303342&amp;usg=AOvVaw0rQiwvb12xV-i0UuMJrCkg">mentioned</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;in the Circuit Training repo. </span>
<span class="c42 c32">All results are for DRC-clean final routing produced by the Innovus tool.</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c34 c97 c70 c40">[In the immediately-following content, we also show comparison results using other macro placement methods, collected since August 18.]</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c34 c70 c40">[As of August 24 onward, we refer to this testcase as &ldquo;</span>
<span class="c42 c70 c40 c32">Our Ariane133-NanGate45_51</span>
<span class="c34 c70 c40">&rdquo; since it has 51% area utilization. A second testcase, &ldquo;</span>
<span class="c42 c70 c40 c32">Our Ariane133-NanGate45_68</span>
<span class="c34 c97 c70 c40">&rdquo;, has 68% area utilization which exactly matches that of the Ariane in Circuit Training.] </span>
</p>

<span class="c42 c32">Comparison 3: </span>
<span class="c85 c42 c32">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://vlsicad.ucsd.edu/Publications/Conferences/389/c389.pdf&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420350546&amp;usg=AOvVaw20ZcVldQS8NpjnBalLoYt2">RTL-MP</a>

</span>

<span class="c42 c32">Comparison 4: </span>
<span class="c34">The Hier-RTLMP macro placer was run on the same (flat) netlist with the same canvas size and I/O placement, with results as follows. <a id="id.2m4eguqpzaee">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">August 20: </span>
<span class="c34 c70 c40">Matching the area utilization.</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;We revisited the area utilization of Our Ariane133 and realized that it (51%) is lower than that of Google&rsquo;s Ariane (68%). So that this would not devalue our study, we created a second variant, </span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">&nbsp;&ldquo;Our Ariane133-NanGate45_68&rdquo;</span>
<span class="c35 c34">, which matches the area utilization of Google&rsquo;s Ariane. Results are as given below.</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47 c27">
<span class="c2">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">Circuit Training Baseline</span>
<sup>
<a href="#cmnt2" id="cmnt_ref2">[b]</a>
</sup>
<sup>
<a href="#cmnt3" id="cmnt_ref3">[c]</a>
</sup>
<sup>
<a href="#cmnt4" id="cmnt_ref4">[d]</a>
</sup>

<span class="c42 c40 c117 c32">_68</span>
<span class="c35 c42 c32">&rdquo;. </span>
</p>

<p class="c8">
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 211.20px; height: 194.30px;">
<img alt="" src="images/image22.png" style="width: 211.20px; height: 194.30px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);" title="">
</span>
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 211.20px; height: 194.30px;">
<img alt="" src="images/image18.png" style="width: 211.20px; height: 194.30px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);" title="">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c42 c32">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">August 25: </span>
<span class="c34 c70 c40">Replication of the congestion component of proxy cost.</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;Reverse-engineering from the plc client API is finally completed, as described </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1hM7UbmANkhoGB3-UfFBp8TRDvvVjpmio7cyyjK4a5bI/edit?usp%3Dsharing&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420479591&amp;usg=AOvVaw12-4fYBfUWwzcziUrt9AVp">here</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">. A review with Dr. Mustafa Yazgan was very helpful in confirming the case analysis and conventions identified during reverse-engineering. &nbsp;Replication results are shown below. &nbsp;With this, reproduction in open </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/CodeElements/Plc_client&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420479954&amp;usg=AOvVaw3kUrxBKWSoMbxH94LPRdbk">source code</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c40">&nbsp;of the Circuit Training proxy cost has been completed. &nbsp;Note that the description </span>
<span class="c12 c40">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://docs.google.com/document/d/1hM7UbmANkhoGB3-UfFBp8TRDvvVjpmio7cyyjK4a5bI/edit?usp%3Dsharing&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420480220&amp;usg=AOvVaw15DkFU8ux3RCs5KQSoFoy5">here</a>
</span>
<span class="c42 c32">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34">illustrates how the Nature paper, Circuit Training, and Google engineers&rsquo; versions can have minor discrepancies. (These minor discrepancies are not currently viewed as substantive, i.e., meaningfully affecting our ongoing assessment.) For example, to calculate the congestion component, the H- and V-routing congestion cost lists are concatenated, and the ABU5 (average of top 5% of the concatenated list) metric of this list is the congestion cost. By contrast, the Nature paper indicates use of an ABU10 metric. Recall: &ldquo;</span>
<span class="c34 c92 c58">There is no substitute for source code.&rdquo;</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c34">&nbsp;</span>

<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c67 c32 c77">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47 c27">
<span class="c2">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32">August 26: </span>
<span class="c34 c70 c40">Moving on to understand benefits and limitations of the Circuit Training methodology itself.</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;This next stage of study is enabled by confidence in the technical solidity of what has been accomplished so far &ndash; again, with the help of Google engineers.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.nje71pf7y0gy">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c70 c40 c32">Question 1.</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;How does having an initial set of placement locations (from physical synthesis) affect the (relative) quality of the CT result? &nbsp;</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c34 c92 c40 c58">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c34 c40 c58">A preliminary exercise has compared outcomes when the Genus iSpatial (x,y) coordinates are given, versus when vacuous (x,y) coordinates are given. The following CT result is for the </span>
<span class="c42 c40 c58 c32">&ldquo;Our Ariane133-NanGate45_68&rdquo;</span>
<span class="c34 c40 c58">&nbsp;example where the input protobuf netlist to Circuit Training&rsquo;s grouping code has all macro and standard cell locations </span>
<span class="c34 c40 c58">set to (600, 600). </span>
<span class="c34 c40 c58 c92">This is just an exercise for now: other, carefully-designed experiments will be performed over the coming weeks and months.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47 c27">
<span class="c2">
</span>
</p>
<a id="t.0a3b8e967f0975380e89fb9c0d82192a451312e6">

<p class="c8">
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 211.20px; height: 193.25px;">

</span>
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 211.20px; height: 191.14px;">
<img alt="" src="images/image36.png" style="width: 211.20px; height: 191.14px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);" title="">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c70 c40 c58 c32">Update to Question 1 on September 9:</span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34 c40">Two additional vacuous placements were run through the CT flow.</span>
</p>
<ul class="c61 lst-kix_ww92s9u94nm-0 start">
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c97 c45">Place all macros and standard cells at the lower left corner i.e., (0, 0).</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c45">Place all macros and standard cells at the upper right corner, i.e., (max_x, max_y), </span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;where </span>
<span class="c34 c97 c45">max_x = 1347.1 and max_y = 1346.8.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c29 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c45">(0, 0) gives us the best (by a small amount) result among the three vacuous placements. </span>
<span class="c34 c58 c45">It has been requested that we report variances and p values. We are unsure how to resource such a request. </span>
<span class="c34 c45">Note that the original baseline result </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.c1dzktk856x2">here</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c97 c45">, using the (x,y) information from physical synthesis, achieves a final routed wirelength of 4295572, around 7% better than the (0, 0) result.</span>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c34 c97 c45">
</span>

<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c70 c40 c32">Question 2.</span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c35 c34">How does utilization affect the (relative) performance of CT?</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.dj2y5i3y3fc5">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c70 c40 c32">Question 3.</span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c35 c34">&nbsp;Is a testcase such as Ariane-133 &ldquo;probative&rdquo;, or do we need better testcases?</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c34 c40 c58">A preliminary exercise has examined Innovus P&amp;R outcomes when the Circuit Training macro placement locations for Our Ariane133-NanGate45_68 are</span>
<span class="c34 c40 c58">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c42 c40 c58 c32">randomly shuffled</span>
<span class="c34 c40 c58">.</span>
<sup>
<a href="#cmnt12" id="cmnt_ref12">[l]</a>
</sup>

</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>

<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c35 c42 c32">September 9: </span>
</p>
<ul class="c61 lst-kix_rleiipw8yujd-0 start">
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34">We have added two more vacuous initial placements to the study of </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.nje71pf7y0gy">Question 1</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">. </span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c47 c84 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34">We have added an initial study of impact from placement guidance to clustering. See </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.97vrrdib4d6w">Question 4</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">.</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp; </span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34">We have taken a look at the impact of Coordinate Descent on proxy cost and on Table 1 metrics. See </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.vxma5fbo0ge8">Question 5</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34">We have obtained a data point to compare two alternate Cadence flows for obtaining the initial macro placement. &nbsp;See </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.b6piompwtbeq">Question 6</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34">We have taken a look at a potential new baseline, which is simply to let the commercial physical synthesis / P&amp;R tool flow run until the end of routing, without any involvement of CT. &nbsp;See </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.yp0ac5r1mfth">Question 7</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34">We have obtained an initial CT result on a second testcase, NVDLA, </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.jy99x07wvut9">here</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">.</span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c36 c34">As this running log is becoming unwieldy, we propose to pin a summary of questions and conclusions to date at the bottom of this document. &nbsp;We will also add this into our GitHub, as planned. &nbsp;And, we request that questions and experimental requests be posed as GitHub issues, and that the limited bandwidth and resources of students be taken into account when making these requests. </span>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.97vrrdib4d6w">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c70 c40 c32">Question 4. </span>
<span class="c34">How much does the </span>
<span class="c42 c32">guidance to clustering</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;that comes from (x,y) locations matter?</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c34">We answer this by using hMETIS to generate the same number of soft macros from the same netlist, but only via the </span>
<span class="c34 c58">npart</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;(number of partitions) parameter. The value of </span>
<span class="c34 c58">npart </span>
<span class="c34">in the call to hMETIS is chosen to match the number of standard-cell clusters (i.e., soft macros) obtained in the CT grouping process. Then, to preserve this number of soft macros, we skip the </span>
<span class="c85 c42 c32">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/b9f53c25ccdb8e588b12d09bf2b1c94bfa1c2b89/circuit_training/grouping/grouping.py%23L721&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420609914&amp;usg=AOvVaw10zbiFXym6CYvZFZ3I7E64">break up</a>
</span>
<span class="c42 c32">&nbsp;and </span>
<span class="c85 c42 c32">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/b9f53c25ccdb8e588b12d09bf2b1c94bfa1c2b89/circuit_training/grouping/grouping.py%23L598&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420610386&amp;usg=AOvVaw3FK268hiSM6e8O1yLRQzTi">merge</a>
</span>
<sup>
<a href="#cmnt13" id="cmnt_ref13">[m]</a>
</sup>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;stage in CT grouping.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c34 c36">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c74">[Brief overview of break up and merge: &nbsp;(A) </span>
<span class="c68">Break up:</span>
<span class="c74">&nbsp;During break up, if a standard cell cluster height or width is greater than </span>
<span class="c68 c168 c58">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/6a76e327a70b5f0c9e3291b57c085688386da04e/circuit_training/grouping/grouper.py%23L138&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420611056&amp;usg=AOvVaw2QSppqhNRymxBhVFytwKUw">sqrt(canvas area / 16)</a>
</span>
<span class="c74">,</span>
<span class="c74">&nbsp;then it is broken into small clusters such that the height and width of each cluster is less than </span>
<span class="c74 c58">sqrt(canvas area / 16)</span>
<span class="c74">. &nbsp;(B) </span>
<span class="c68">Merge:</span>
<span class="c74">&nbsp;During merge, if the number of standard cells is less than the </span>
<span class="c68 c168">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/6a76e327a70b5f0c9e3291b57c085688386da04e/circuit_training/grouping/grouper.py%23L178&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420611572&amp;usg=AOvVaw3BPrXYd0IEZ5htOlOhiaCo">(average number of standard cells in a cluster / 4)</a>
</span>
<span class="c74">, then the standard cells of that cluster are moved to t</span>
<span class="c74">heir neighboring</span>
<sup>
<a href="#cmnt14" id="cmnt_ref14">[n]</a>
</sup>
<sup>
<a href="#cmnt15" id="cmnt_ref15">[o]</a>
</sup>
<span class="c74">&nbsp;clusters.]</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c34">We run hMETIS with </span>
<span class="c34 c58">npart </span>
<span class="c34">= 810 (number of fixed groups is 153) to match the total number of standard cell clusters when CT&rsquo;s break up and merge is run. The following table presents the results of this experiment. Outcomes are similar to the original </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.2m4eguqpzaee">Ariane133-NG45 with 68% utilization CT result</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">. &nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34 c92 c58">[The Question 1 study indicates that a vacuous placement harms the outcome of CT, i.e., &ldquo;placement information matters&rdquo;. But the Question 4 study suggests that a flow that does not bring in any placement coordinates (i.e., using pure hMETIS partitioning down to a similar number of stdcell clusters) does not affect results by much.]</span>
</p>
<p class="c52 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c39">
</span>
</p>
<a id="t.96931da07df8de13909f1f9ca05ec26c7b2c5fc6">
</a>

</p>

</span>
</p>
<a id="id.vxma5fbo0ge8">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c40 c32 c70">Question 5. </span>
<span class="c36 c34">What is the impact of the Coordinate Descent (CD) placer on proxy cost and Table 1 metric?</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c34">In our </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.gil8up925m8u">August 18</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;notes, we mentioned that </span>
<span class="c34">the default CT flow does NOT run coordinate descent. (Coordinate descent is not mentioned in the Nature paper.) The </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/main/docs/ARIANE.md%23results&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420630948&amp;usg=AOvVaw33vK5blClb0KaFE4IVwrBL">result in the CT repo</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">&nbsp;shows the impact of Coordinate Descent (CD) on proxy cost for the Google Ariane design, but there is no data to show the impact of CD on Table 1 metrics.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c36 c34">We have taken the CT results generated for Ariane133-NG45 with 68% utilization through the CD placement step. The following table shows the effect of CD placer on proxy cost. The CD placer for this instance improves proxy wirelength and density at the cost of congestion, and overall proxy cost degrades slightly.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<a id="t.b94543b063d4142bd91029066038de367013a509">

<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c39">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c36 c34">Even though CD improves proxy wirelength, the post-route wirelength worsens slightly (by ~1.47%) compared to the original CT macro placement.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.b6piompwtbeq">
</a>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c42 c70 c32">Question 6.</span>
<span class="c42 c32">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c36 c34">Are we using the industry tool in an &ldquo;expert&rdquo; manner? &nbsp;(We believe so.)</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c36 c34">We received an inquiry regarding the multiple ways in which macro placements could be obtained using Cadence tooling. &nbsp; To clarify:</span>
</p>
<ul class="c61 lst-kix_26n6gq4t3wd2-0 start">
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c45">In our previous CT result shown </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="#id.2m4eguqpzaee">here</a>
</span>
<span class="c34 c97 c45">, the initial macro placement (which is fed into Genus iSpatial) is generated using Innovus Concurrent Macro Placer. </span>
</li>
<li class="c13 c84 c47 li-bullet-0">
<span class="c34 c45">It is also possible to use Genus iSpatial to perform </span>
<span class="c42 c45 c32">both </span>
<span class="c34 c97 c45">macro and standard-cell placement. In our experience, this worsens results, as shown below. &nbsp;I.e., based on our current understanding, the macro placement produced by Innovus Concurrent Macro Placer leads to the best results when fed to the CT flow.</span>
</li>
</ul>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c39 c97 c45">
</span>
</p>
<a id="t.e0fba47329b728486eb019486796dc27ef921424">
</a>
<a id="t.23">
</a>

</p>
</td>

<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 188.00px; height: 194.13px;">

</span>
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 188.50px; height: 195.03px;">
<img alt="" src="images/image6.png" style="width: 188.50px; height: 195.03px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);" title="">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c34 c97 c45">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.yp0ac5r1mfth">
</a>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c42 c70 c32">Question 7.</span>
<span class="c42 c45 c32">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34 c45">What happens if we skip CT and continue </span>
<span class="c42 c45 c32">directly </span>
<span class="c34 c97 c45">to standard-cell P&amp;R (i.e., the Innovus 21.1 flow) once we have a macro placement from the commercial tool?</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c34 c97 c45">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c34 c45">At some point during the past weeks, we realized that this would also be a potential &ldquo;baseline&rdquo; for comparison. As can be seen below for both 68% and 51% variants of Ariane-133 in NG45, omitting the CT step can also produce good results by the Table 1 metrics. </span>
<span class="c34 c70">At this point, we do </span>
<span class="c42 c70 c32">not </span>
<span class="c34 c70">have any diagnosis or interpretation of this data.</span>
<span class="c34 c97 c45">&nbsp;One possible implication is that the Ariane-133 testcase is in some way not probative. &nbsp;The community&rsquo;s suggestions (e.g., alternate testcases, constraints, floorplan setup, etc.) are always welcome. </span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c1">
</span>
</p>

<span class="c36 c39">Ariane 68%:</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span>&nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp; &nbsp;</span>
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 199.74px; height: 159.97px;">
<img alt="" src="images/image8.png" style="width: 199.74px; height: 159.97px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);" title="">
</span>
<span style="overflow: hidden; display: inline-block; margin: 0.00px 0.00px; border: 0.00px solid #000000; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); width: 190.63px; height: 159.36px;">
<img alt="" src="images/image2.png" style="width: 190.63px; height: 159.36px; margin-left: 0.00px; margin-top: 0.00px; transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px); -webkit-transform: rotate(0.00rad) translateZ(0px);" title="">
</span>

<span class="c34 c97 c45">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.lhytkh968x59">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c42 c70 c40 c32">Question 8.</span>
<span class="c42 c40 c32">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c35 c34">How does the tightness of timing constraints affect the (relative) performance of CT? &nbsp;</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c35 c34">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c34 c40">[Comment: This is related to Question 2, and is part of the broad question of field of use / sweet spot. &nbsp;We still intend to work in the space of {design testcase} X {technology and design enablement} X {utilization} X {performance requirement}X experimental {questions, design/setup, execution} to reach conclusions that are above the bar of &ldquo;satisfying readers&rdquo;. Progress will continue to be reported here and in GitHub.]</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c29 c27">
<span class="c2">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c27 c29">
<span class="c36 c39">
</span>
</p>
<a id="id.jy99x07wvut9">
</a>
<p class="c13 c29">
<span class="c35 c42 c32">Circuit Training Baseline Result on &ldquo;Our NVDLA-NanGate45_68&rdquo;. </span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c39">
</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47">
<span class="c34">We have trained CT to generate a macro placement for the </span>
<span class="c34 c168">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/TILOS-AI-Institute/MacroPlacement/tree/main/Flows/NanGate45/nvdla&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420697417&amp;usg=AOvVaw0cV7Ve0RQIuZp8awnq6D8U">NVDLA design</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">.</span>
<span class="c42 c32">&nbsp;</span>
<span class="c34">For this experiment we use</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;the NanGate45 enablement; the initial canvas size is generated by setting utilization to 68%. We use the default hyperparameters used for Ariane to train CT for NVDLA design. The number of hard macros in NVDLA is 128, so we update </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/6a76e327a70b5f0c9e3291b57c085688386da04e/circuit_training/learning/ppo_collect.py%23L53&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420697927&amp;usg=AOvVaw3a8PK96-Hl-1vVA-8j9MoA">max_sequnece_length</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;to 129 in </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/6a76e327a70b5f0c9e3291b57c085688386da04e/circuit_training/learning/ppo_collect.py%23L53&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420698271&amp;usg=AOvVaw3btyFrlyKPtP9p2BDMda5w">ppo_collect.py</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp; and </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/6a76e327a70b5f0c9e3291b57c085688386da04e/circuit_training/learning/train_ppo.py%23L57&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420698612&amp;usg=AOvVaw1TGQlWkc1g47at-1Iph4yS">sequence_length</a>
</span>
<span class="c34">&nbsp;to 129 in </span>
<span class="c12">
<a class="c24" href="https://www.google.com/url?q=https://github.com/google-research/circuit_training/blob/6a76e327a70b5f0c9e3291b57c085688386da04e/circuit_training/learning/train_ppo.py%23L57&amp;sa=D&amp;source=editors&amp;ust=1663419420698933&amp;usg=AOvVaw3TPAkKqltBSRUgvdvM7roJ">train_ppo.py</a>
</span>
<span class="c36 c34">.</span>
</p>
<p class="c13 c47 c27">
<span class="c36 c34">
</span>
</p>

<p class="c13 c29">
